.cs1-kern-left,.mw-parser-output .cs1-kern-wl-left{padding-left:0.2em}.mw-parser-output .cs1-kern-right,.mw-parser-output .cs1-kern-wl-right{padding-right:0.2em}.mw-parser-output .citation .mw-selflink{font-weight:inherit}</style><cite class="citation web cs1"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.london-luton.co.uk/CMSPages/GetFile.aspx?guid=7f219cda-8c6f-4b36-9b41-8ebbf2bf09b7">"2010 to 2017 Statistics"</a>. London Luton Airport.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=2010+to+2017+Statistics&amp;rft.pub=London+Luton+Airport&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.london-luton.co.uk%2FCMSPages%2FGetFile.aspx%3Fguid%3D7f219cda-8c6f-4b36-9b41-8ebbf2bf09b7&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ALuton+Airport" class="Z3988"></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>London Luton Airport</b> (<a href="/wiki/IATA_airport_code" title="IATA airport code">IATA</a>: <b>LTN</b>, <a href="/wiki/ICAO_airport_code" title="ICAO airport code">ICAO</a>: <b>EGGW</b>), previously called <i>Luton International Airport</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-history_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> is an <a href="/wiki/International_airport" title="International airport">international airport</a> located 1.5 <a href="/wiki/Mile" title="Mile">miles</a> (2.4&#160;km) east of <a href="/wiki/Luton" title="Luton">Luton</a> town centre in England,<sup id="cite_ref-aip_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aip-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> and is 28 miles (45&#160;km) north of <a href="/wiki/Central_London" title="Central London">Central London</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-aip_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aip-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> The airport is owned by London Luton Airport Ltd (LLAL), a company wholly owned by <a href="/wiki/Luton_Borough_Council" title="Luton Borough Council">Luton Borough Council</a>, and operated by London Luton Airport Operations Ltd (LLAOL).<sup id="cite_ref-LLAL_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LLAL-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ownership_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ownership-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>An airport was opened on the site on 16 July 1938.<sup id="cite_ref-80th_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80th-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">Second World War</a>, the airport was used by fighters of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Air_Force" title="Royal Air Force">Royal Air Force</a>. Commercial activity and <a href="/wiki/General_aviation" title="General aviation">general aviation</a> flight training at Luton resumed during 1952. By the 1960s, Luton Airport was playing a key role in the development of the <a href="/wiki/Package_holiday" class="mw-redirect" title="Package holiday">package holiday</a> business; by 1969, a fifth of all holiday flights from the UK departed from Luton Airport. From the mid-1960s, <a href="/wiki/Business_aircraft" title="Business aircraft">executive aircraft</a> have been based at the airport. During the late 1970s, an expansion plan was initiated at Luton to accommodate as many as 5 million passengers per year, although the airport experienced a reduction in passenger numbers in the 1980s. In 1990, the airport was renamed <i>London Luton Airport</i> to re-emphasise the airport\'s proximity to the capital.\n</p><p>The arrival of new operators at Luton during the 1990s, such as <a href="/wiki/Charter_flight" class="mw-redirect" title="Charter flight">charter operator</a> <a href="/wiki/MyTravel_Group" title="MyTravel Group">MyTravel Group</a> and new <a href="/wiki/Low-cost_carrier" title="Low-cost carrier">low-cost</a> scheduled flights from <a href="/wiki/Debonair_(airline)" title="Debonair (airline)">Debonair</a> and <a href="/wiki/EasyJet" title="EasyJet">EasyJet</a>, contributed to a rapid increase in passenger numbers that made it the fastest growing major airport in the UK. In August 1997, to fund an \xc2\xa380&#160;million extension of the airport, a 30-year concession contract was issued to a <a href="/wiki/Public-private_partnership" class="mw-redirect" title="Public-private partnership">public-private partnership</a> consortium, <i>London Luton Airport Operations Limited</i>. Throughout the 1990s, \xc2\xa330 million was invested in Luton\'s infrastructure and facilities. In November 1999, a new \xc2\xa340 million terminal was opened by <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Queen Elizabeth II</a> and <a href="/wiki/Prince_Philip,_Duke_of_Edinburgh" title="Prince Philip, Duke of Edinburgh">Prince Philip</a>; the new building houses 60 check-in desks, baggage and flight information systems and a range of commercial outlets. During 2004/5, the departure and arrivals lounges and other facilities were redeveloped at a cost of \xc2\xa338 million.\n</p><p>In 2018, over 16.5 million passengers passed through the airport, a record total for Luton making it the <a href="/wiki/Busiest_airports_in_the_United_Kingdom_by_total_passenger_traffic" class="mw-redirect" title="Busiest airports in the United Kingdom by total passenger traffic">fifth \nbusiest airport</a> in the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-stats_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stats-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> It is the fourth-largest airport serving the London area after <a href="/wiki/Heathrow_Airport" title="Heathrow Airport">Heathrow</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gatwick_Airport" title="Gatwick Airport">Gatwick</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stansted_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Stansted Airport">Stansted</a>, and is one of London\'s six international airports along with <a href="/wiki/London_City_Airport" title="London City Airport">London City</a> and <a href="/wiki/Southend_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Southend Airport">Southend</a>. The airport serves as a base for <a href="/wiki/EasyJet" title="EasyJet">EasyJet</a>, <a href="/wiki/TUI_Airways" title="TUI Airways">TUI Airways</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ryanair" title="Ryanair">Ryanair</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wizz_Air" title="Wizz Air">Wizz Air</a> and previously served as a base for <a href="/wiki/Monarch_Airlines" title="Monarch Airlines">Monarch Airlines</a> until it ceased operations in October 2017. The vast majority of the routes served are within Europe, although there are some charter and scheduled routes to destinations in Northern Africa and Asia.\n</p><p>The airport is two miles from Junction 10 of the <a href="/wiki/M1_motorway" title="M1 motorway">M1 motorway</a>. Trains between <a href="/wiki/St_Pancras_railway_station" title="St Pancras railway station">St Pancras station</a> in Central London and <a href="/wiki/Luton_Airport_Parkway_railway_station" title="Luton Airport Parkway railway station">Luton Airport Parkway railway station</a> take 22 minutes on the fastest train and an average of 32 minutes.<sup id="cite_ref-auto1_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> There is a 10-minute shuttle-bus between the railway station and the airport terminal;<sup id="cite_ref-auto1_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> it is scheduled to be replaced by the <a href="/wiki/Luton_DART" title="Luton DART">Luton DART</a> <a href="/wiki/Automated_people_mover" class="mw-redirect" title="Automated people mover">automated people mover</a> by 2021.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toclevel-1 tocsection-23"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">13</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Luton_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_history">Early history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Luton_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Early history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Luton Municipal Airport was opened on the site on 16 July 1938 by the <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_State_for_Air" title="Secretary of State for Air">Secretary of State for Air</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingsley_Wood" title="Kingsley Wood">Kingsley Wood</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-history_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bbc-80th_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-80th-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> Situated where the valley of the <a href="/wiki/River_Lea" title="River Lea">River Lea</a> cuts its way through the north-east end of the <a href="/wiki/Chiltern_Hills" title="Chiltern Hills">Chiltern Hills</a>, the airport occupies a hill-top location, with a roughly 40&#160;m (130&#160;ft) drop-off at the western end of the <a href="/wiki/Runway" title="Runway">runway</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-osexp1_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-osexp1-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-osexp2_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-osexp2-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> The airport, which was owned by the <a href="/wiki/Borough_of_Luton" class="mw-redirect" title="Borough of Luton">Borough of Luton</a>, was considered to be the northern terminal for neighbouring <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-guide_hist_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guide_hist-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>During the <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">Second World War</a>, the airport was used by the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Air_Force" title="Royal Air Force">Royal Air Force</a>, fighters of <a href="/wiki/No._264_Squadron_RAF" title="No. 264 Squadron RAF">No. 264 Squadron</a> being based there.<sup id="cite_ref-guide_hist_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guide_hist-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Following the end of the conflict, the site was returned to the local council. During 1952, activity at the airport resumed on a commercial basis; a new <a href="/wiki/Control_tower" class="mw-redirect" title="Control tower">control tower</a> was opened around this time.<sup id="cite_ref-guide_hist_15-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guide_hist-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>British aviation company <a href="/wiki/Percival_Aircraft" class="mw-redirect" title="Percival Aircraft">Percival Aircraft</a> had its factory at the airport until the early 1960s. From the mid-1960s, <a href="/wiki/Business_aircraft" title="Business aircraft">executive aircraft</a> have been based at the airport, initially operated by McAlpine Aviation. These activities have grown and several executive jet operators and maintenance companies are currently based at Luton.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>By the 1960s, Luton Airport was playing a key role in the development of the <a href="/wiki/Package_holiday" class="mw-redirect" title="Package holiday">package holiday</a> business, the popularity of the foreign holiday had risen dramatically as the launch of new services had allowed greater numbers of people to travel abroad for the first time.<sup id="cite_ref-guide_hist_15-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guide_hist-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Luton became the operating base for several <a href="/wiki/Charter_airline" class="mw-redirect" title="Charter airline">charter airlines</a>, such as <a href="/wiki/Court_Line#Autair" title="Court Line">Autair</a> (which went on to become <a href="/wiki/Court_Line#Court_Line" title="Court Line">Court Line</a>), <a href="/wiki/Britannia_Airways" title="Britannia Airways">Euravia</a> (now <a href="/wiki/TUI_Airways" title="TUI Airways">TUI Airways</a>, following Euravia\'s change of name to <a href="/wiki/Britannia_Airways" title="Britannia Airways">Britannia Airways</a> and subsequent merger with <a href="/wiki/First_Choice_Airways" title="First Choice Airways">First Choice Airways</a> and TUI rebrand) and <a href="/wiki/Dan-Air" title="Dan-Air">Dan-Air</a>.\n</p><p>By 1969, a fifth of all holiday flights from the UK departed from Luton Airport; during 1972, Luton Airport was the most profitable airport in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-guide_hist_15-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guide_hist-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> However, Luton suffered a severe setback in August 1974 when major <a href="/wiki/Package_holiday" class="mw-redirect" title="Package holiday">package holiday</a> operator <a href="/wiki/Clarksons_Travel_Group" title="Clarksons Travel Group">Clarksons</a> and its in-house airline <a href="/wiki/Court_Line" title="Court Line">Court Line</a> (which also operated coach links) ceased operations and were <a href="/wiki/Liquidation" title="Liquidation">liquidated</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-history_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> Nevertheless, by 1978, the airport\'s management initiated an expansion plan as to allow Luton to accommodate as many as 5 million passengers per year.<sup id="cite_ref-guide_hist_15-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guide_hist-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1980s_and_1990s">1980s and 1990s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Luton_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 1980s and 1990s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:LondonLutonAirportOriginal.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/51/LondonLutonAirportOriginal.svg/220px-LondonLutonAirportOriginal.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="111" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/51/LondonLutonAirportOriginal.svg/330px-LondonLutonAirportOriginal.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/51/LondonLutonAirportOriginal.svg/440px-LondonLutonAirportOriginal.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="444" data-file-height="225" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:LondonLutonAirportOriginal.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The airport\'s logo 2001\xe2\x80\x932005</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Luton_Airport_logo.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/7/7b/Luton_Airport_logo.svg/220px-Luton_Airport_logo.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="80" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/7/7b/Luton_Airport_logo.svg/330px-Luton_Airport_logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/7/7b/Luton_Airport_logo.svg/440px-Luton_Airport_logo.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="187" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Luton_Airport_logo.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The airport\'s logo 2005\xe2\x80\x932014</div></div></div>\n<p>During the 1980s, the airport experienced a decline in customer numbers; this was due to lack of reinvestment while the nearby <a href="/wiki/Stansted_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Stansted Airport">Stansted Airport</a>, which was also located north of London, was growing. The council responded to lobbying and focused again on developing the airport. During 1985, a new international terminal building was opened by <a href="/wiki/Prince_of_Wales" title="Prince of Wales">The Prince of Wales</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-guide_hist_15-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guide_hist-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Further updates and changes over the following 15 years were made, including the opening of a new international terminal an automated baggage handling facility, a new control tower with updated air traffic control systems, a new cargo centre and runway upgrades. In 1987, Luton Airport became a <a href="/wiki/Limited_company" title="Limited company">limited company</a>, of which Luton Borough Council was the sole shareholder; this reorganisation was taken as it was felt that the airport ought to be operated at arm\'s length via an independent management team.<sup id="cite_ref-guide_hist_15-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guide_hist-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>While developing the basic infrastructure, various business partners were courted and business models were considered. The process envisaged a cargo centre, an airport railway station, and people mover from station to airport terminal (hence the unused underpass parallel to the road as one approaches the terminal).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> During 1991, an attempt was made to sell Luton Airport, but it was unsuccessful; instead, a new management team was appointed to turn around the business, stem the losses, and improve passenger numbers. Over the following five years, \xc2\xa330 million was invested in Luton\'s infrastructure and facilities.<sup id="cite_ref-guide_hist_15-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guide_hist-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Originally, the airport\'s runways had been grass tracks 18/36 and 06/24, and then a concrete runway 08/26. By the end of the 1980s, there was only one runway, 08/26. The 18/36 grass runway had disappeared under a <a href="/wiki/Landfill" title="Landfill">landfill</a>, while 06/24 had effectively become a <a href="/wiki/Taxiway" title="Taxiway">taxiway</a>. For Luton to maintain viability, it was necessary to update airfield services, and achieve <a href="/wiki/Instrument_landing_system#ILS_categories" title="Instrument landing system">CAT III</a> status. This meant updating the <a href="/wiki/Instrument_landing_system" title="Instrument landing system">instrument landing system</a> (ILS); glidepath and localiser and removing the hump in the runway; even a six-foot person could not see one end of the runway from the other. The hump was removed by building up layers at the end of the runway; this was done over 72 successive nights between October 1988 and February 1989, with the height being raised 90&#160;mm on one particular night. During the course of this work, the airport would re-open for flights during the day.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>In 1990, the airport was renamed <i>London Luton Airport</i> to re-emphasise the airport\'s proximity to the UK capital.<sup id="cite_ref-guide_hist_15-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guide_hist-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> In 1991, another setback occurred when <a href="/wiki/Ryanair" title="Ryanair">Ryanair</a>, which had flown from the airport to <a href="/wiki/Ireland" title="Ireland">Ireland</a> for a number of years, transferred its London operating base from Luton to rival Stansted. This move was attributed as causing a decline in passenger numbers at Luton.<sup id="cite_ref-guide_hist_15-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guide_hist-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Later in the 1990s, <a href="/wiki/MyTravel_Group" title="MyTravel Group">MyTravel Group</a> began <a href="/wiki/Charter_flight" class="mw-redirect" title="Charter flight">charter flights</a> from the airport, using the <i><a href="/wiki/Airtours_International_Airways" class="mw-redirect" title="Airtours International Airways">Airtours</a></i> brand and new <a href="/wiki/Low-cost_carrier" title="Low-cost carrier">low-cost</a> scheduled flights from <a href="/wiki/Debonair_(airline)" title="Debonair (airline)">Debonair</a> and <a href="/wiki/EasyJet" title="EasyJet">EasyJet</a>, the latter making Luton its base.<sup id="cite_ref-history_5-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> The arrival of these new operators marked a rapid increase in passenger numbers; during 1997/1998, 3.4 million people travelled via the airport, while 4.4 million travellers were recording during the following year, making Luton Airport the fastest growing major airport in the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-guide_hist_15-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guide_hist-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In August 1997, to fund an \xc2\xa380&#160;million extension of the airport, the council issued a 30-year concession contract to a <a href="/wiki/Public-private_partnership" class="mw-redirect" title="Public-private partnership">public-private partnership</a> consortium, London Luton Airport Operations Limited, a partnership of Airport Group International (AGI) and <a href="/wiki/Barclays" title="Barclays">Barclays</a> Private Equity. AGI was a specialist airport management and development company once owned by <a href="/wiki/Lockheed_Martin" title="Lockheed Martin">Lockheed Martin</a>. In 1999, AGI was sold to <a href="/wiki/TBI_plc" title="TBI plc">TBI plc</a>; in 2001, Barclays also sold its shares in Luton to TBI plc.<sup id="cite_ref-history_5-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The main feature of the development phase in 1998 was a \xc2\xa340&#160;million terminal made from aluminium and glass, based on an original design by <a href="/wiki/Foster_%2B_Partners" class="mw-redirect" title="Foster + Partners">Foster + Partners</a>. The new terminal, which was officially opened in November 1999 by <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Queen Elizabeth II</a> and <a href="/wiki/Prince_Philip,_Duke_of_Edinburgh" title="Prince Philip, Duke of Edinburgh">Prince Philip</a>, houses 60 check-in desks, baggage and flight information systems and a wide range of shops, restaurants and bars.<sup id="cite_ref-history_5-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> During late 1999, British railway infrastructure company <a href="/wiki/Railtrack" title="Railtrack">Railtrack</a> opened the new <a href="/wiki/Luton_Airport_Parkway_railway_station" title="Luton Airport Parkway railway station">Luton Airport Parkway railway station</a>; built at a cost of \xc2\xa323 million, the station facilitated a travel time to central London of less than 30 minutes.<sup id="cite_ref-guide_hist_15-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guide_hist-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Development_since_the_2000s">Development since the 2000s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Luton_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Development since the 2000s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Luton_Airport_-_geograph.org.uk_-_560676.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Luton_Airport_-_geograph.org.uk_-_560676.jpg/220px-Luton_Airport_-_geograph.org.uk_-_560676.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="108" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Luton_Airport_-_geograph.org.uk_-_560676.jpg/330px-Luton_Airport_-_geograph.org.uk_-_560676.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Luton_Airport_-_geograph.org.uk_-_560676.jpg/440px-Luton_Airport_-_geograph.org.uk_-_560676.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="313" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Luton_Airport_-_geograph.org.uk_-_560676.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The terminal exterior prior to its major expansion</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Luton_airport3.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Luton_airport3.JPG/220px-Luton_airport3.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Luton_airport3.JPG/330px-Luton_airport3.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Luton_airport3.JPG/440px-Luton_airport3.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="2736" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Luton_airport3.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Waiting area</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Boarding_gates_and_apron_at_London_Luton_Airport_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1446390.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Boarding_gates_and_apron_at_London_Luton_Airport_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1446390.jpg/220px-Boarding_gates_and_apron_at_London_Luton_Airport_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1446390.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Boarding_gates_and_apron_at_London_Luton_Airport_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1446390.jpg/330px-Boarding_gates_and_apron_at_London_Luton_Airport_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1446390.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Boarding_gates_and_apron_at_London_Luton_Airport_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1446390.jpg/440px-Boarding_gates_and_apron_at_London_Luton_Airport_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1446390.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Boarding_gates_and_apron_at_London_Luton_Airport_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1446390.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Apron</div></div></div>\n<p>In September 2004, Luton Airport embarked on a 10-month project to develop the departure and arrivals lounges and other facilities at a cost of \xc2\xa338 million; this work included a 9,000&#160;sq&#160;ft (800&#160;m<sup>2</sup>) area featuring a spectacular vaulted ceiling was completed with the new terminal, but intended to lie unused until required. On 1 July 2005, the new departure hall opened on schedule, featuring a boarding pier extending 200&#160;m (660&#160;ft) out between the airport\'s north and east <a href="/wiki/Airport_ramp" class="mw-redirect" title="Airport ramp">aprons</a> and relocated security, customs and immigration facilities, as well as an expanded number of boarding gates from the previous number of 19 to 26.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2004, the airport management announced<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> that they supported the government plans to expand the facilities, which included a full-length runway and a new terminal.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> However, local campaign groups, including Luton and District Association for the Control of Aircraft Noise (LADACAN)<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> and Stop Luton Airport Plan (SLAP)<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> opposed the new expansion plans, for reasons including noise pollution and traffic concerns; LADACAN also claimed that various sites, including <a href="/wiki/Someries_Castle" title="Someries Castle">Someries Castle</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Scheduled_Monument" class="mw-redirect" title="Scheduled Monument">Scheduled Monument</a>, would be threatened by the expansion. On 6 July 2007, it was announced that the owners of London Luton Airport had decided to scrap plans to build a second runway and new terminal for financial reasons.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> In order for the airport to expand further, the <a href="/wiki/Department_for_Transport" title="Department for Transport">Department for Transport</a> (DfT) advised the airport authority to use the airport site more efficiently. The DfT supports plans to extend the runway from its current 2,160&#160;m (7,087&#160;ft) length to 3,000&#160;m (9,843&#160;ft) and increase the length of the <a href="/wiki/Taxiway" title="Taxiway">taxiway</a>. A full-length runway would increase airlines\' operational flexibility by enabling the use of aircraft that have a greater <a href="/wiki/Payload_(air_and_space_craft)" class="mw-redirect" title="Payload (air and space craft)">payload</a> capacity and longer <a href="/wiki/Range_(aircraft)" class="mw-redirect" title="Range (aircraft)">range</a> than is currently possible. A longer taxiway would maximise runway use by reducing the need for taxiing aircraft to cross or move along the runway.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>In January 2005, London Luton Airport Operations Limited was acquired by Airport Concessions Development Limited, a company owned by <a href="/wiki/Abertis" title="Abertis">Abertis Infraestructuras</a> (90%) and <a href="/wiki/Aena" class="mw-redirect" title="Aena">Aena Internacional</a> (10%), both Spanish companies. control organisation.<sup id="cite_ref-history_5-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> In November 2013, ownership of London Luton Airport Operations Ltd passed to Aena and <a href="/wiki/Ardian_(company)" title="Ardian (company)">Ardian</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-airport-technology.com_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-airport-technology.com-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> In April 2018, <a href="/wiki/AMP_Capital" title="AMP Capital">AMP Capital</a> acquired Ardian\'s 49% stake in the business.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>By 2006, the last flight training operator had ceased training from the airport.\n</p><p>From 2006 to 2008, <a href="/wiki/Silverjet" title="Silverjet">Silverjet</a> operated long-haul flights to <a href="/wiki/Newark_Liberty_International_Airport" title="Newark Liberty International Airport">Newark</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dubai_International_Airport" title="Dubai International Airport">Dubai</a> from a dedicated terminal, but ceased operations due to the <a href="/wiki/Financial_crisis_of_2007-2008" class="mw-redirect" title="Financial crisis of 2007-2008">global economic crisis</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In September 2016, <a href="/wiki/La_Compagnie" title="La Compagnie">La Compagnie</a> announced it would cease operating its Luton to Newark service citing economic reasons.<sup id="cite_ref-newarkshutdown_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newarkshutdown-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> Therefore, Luton lost its only long-haul service. In February 2017, Hungarian low-cost carrier <a href="/wiki/Wizz_Air" title="Wizz Air">Wizz Air</a> announced it would to open its first British base at Luton Airport inaugurating three new routes to <a href="/wiki/Tel_Aviv" title="Tel Aviv">Tel Aviv</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pristina" title="Pristina">Pristina</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kutaisi" title="Kutaisi">Kutaisi</a><sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> in addition to more than a dozen already served ones from other bases.\n</p><p>During December 2018, a three-year redevelopment of Luton Airport was officially launched. Costing roughly \xc2\xa3160 million, airport management stated that the upgrade, which included new shops, a new boarding pier, and more boarding gates, would increase overall capacity by 50%, enabling the site to accommodate 18 million passengers by 2020. Campaigners from local pressure groups such as LADACAN have complained that the airport had failed to incorporate reduce noise reduction measures into the plan, while an airport spokesperson stated "Our noise control measures are some of the most stringent of any major UK airport" and noted that it has applied for additional flight restrictions.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> In addition, earlier that year, work had commenced on the construction of the <a href="/wiki/Luton_DART" title="Luton DART">Luton DART</a>, an <a href="/wiki/People_mover" title="People mover">automated guided people mover</a> which shall travel between <a href="/wiki/Luton_Airport_Parkway_railway_station" title="Luton Airport Parkway railway station">Luton Airport Parkway station</a> and the airport itself.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-itv-201804_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-itv-201804-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> Costed at \xc2\xa3200 million, the DART shall eliminate the need for shuttle buses by 2021.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Facilities">Facilities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Luton_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Facilities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Control_tower_and_Easyjet_building_-_geograph.org.uk_-_755523.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Control_tower_and_Easyjet_building_-_geograph.org.uk_-_755523.jpg/220px-Control_tower_and_Easyjet_building_-_geograph.org.uk_-_755523.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="109" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Control_tower_and_Easyjet_building_-_geograph.org.uk_-_755523.jpg/330px-Control_tower_and_Easyjet_building_-_geograph.org.uk_-_755523.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Control_tower_and_Easyjet_building_-_geograph.org.uk_-_755523.jpg/440px-Control_tower_and_Easyjet_building_-_geograph.org.uk_-_755523.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="317" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Control_tower_and_Easyjet_building_-_geograph.org.uk_-_755523.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Control tower next to Hangar 89, the <a href="/wiki/EasyJet" title="EasyJet">easyJet</a> head office</div></div></div>\n<p>The airport possesses a single runway, running roughly east to west (07/25),<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> with a length of 2,160&#160;m (7,087&#160;ft)<sup id="cite_ref-aip_6-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aip-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> at an elevation of 526&#160;ft (160&#160;m). The runway is equipped with an <a href="/wiki/Instrument_Landing_System" class="mw-redirect" title="Instrument Landing System">Instrument Landing System</a> (ILS) rated to Category IIIB, allowing the airport to continue operating in conditions of poor visibility.<sup id="cite_ref-techdet_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-techdet-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-comnews0608_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-comnews0608-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>All the airport facilities lie to the north of the runway. The terminal and aprons have a somewhat unusual layout, with ground-side access to the terminal being via a road (which goes under the taxiway) to a bus station, drop off area, taxi rank and short term car park on the runway side of the terminal building. There are approximately 60 stands available for aircraft. All of these stands are located on the northern side of the terminal building, away from the runway and connected to it by a \'U\' shaped set of taxiways and aprons that together encircle the terminal.<sup id="cite_ref-osexp1_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-osexp1-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-osexp2_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-osexp2-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The northern side of the U-shaped apron is ringed by a continuous line of <a href="/wiki/Hangar" title="Hangar">hangars</a> and other buildings, emphasising the fact that Luton is a major maintenance base for several airlines including <a href="/wiki/TUI_Airways" title="TUI Airways">TUI Airways</a>, <a href="/wiki/EasyJet" title="EasyJet">EasyJet</a>, and previously <a href="/wiki/Monarch_Airlines" title="Monarch Airlines">Monarch Airlines</a>. By contrast to the heavily built up apron area, the airport\'s southern boundary is entirely rural with only a few isolated farm buildings and houses close to the airport boundary.<sup id="cite_ref-osexp1_12-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-osexp1-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-osexp2_13-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-osexp2-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The airport remains in municipal ownership, owned by <a href="/wiki/Luton_Borough_Council" title="Luton Borough Council">Luton Borough Council</a> but managed by the private sector London Luton Airport Operations Limited (LLAOL). London Luton Airport has a <a href="/wiki/Civil_Aviation_Authority_(United_Kingdom)" title="Civil Aviation Authority (United Kingdom)">Civil Aviation Authority</a> Public Use Aerodrome Licence (Number P835) that allows flights for the public transport of passengers or for flying instruction. An indicator of the importance of the airport to the economy of Luton is that Luton is reported to have the highest number of taxicabs per head of population in the United Kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>EasyJet\'s head office is Hangar 89 (H89), a building located on the grounds of London Luton Airport; the hangar, a former <a href="/wiki/Britannia_Airways" title="Britannia Airways">Britannia Airways</a>/<a href="/wiki/TUI_Group" title="TUI Group">TUI</a> facility, is located 150 metres (490&#160;ft) from the former site of EasyLand, the previous headquarters of EasyJet. Hangar 89, built in 1974, has 30,000&#160;sq&#160;ft (2,800&#160;m<sup>2</sup>) of office space and can house two aircraft the size of an <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A320_family" title="Airbus A320 family">Airbus A320</a> or <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737" title="Boeing 737">Boeing 737</a> at one time. When EasyJet received H89, it had a 1970s style office setup. EasyJet modernised the building and painted it orange.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In addition, <a href="/wiki/TUI_Airways" title="TUI Airways">TUI Airways</a> head office is at the airport, and - prior to its closure - <a href="/wiki/Monarch_Airlines" title="Monarch Airlines">Monarch Airlines</a>\'s head office, along with that of Monarch Group, was in Prospect House, on the grounds of the airport.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminal">Terminal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Luton_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Terminal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Luton Airport features one single, two-storey passenger terminal building which has been expanded and rearranged several times. The ground floor features a main hall equipped with 62 check-in desks (<i>1-62</i>), a separate security screening hall, as well as some shops, service counters and the arrivals facilities.<sup id="cite_ref-officialmap_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-officialmap-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> After the security screening hall, stairs lead to the departures lounge on the upper floor, where several more stores, restaurants and all 41 departure gates in three side piers (<i>1-19</i>,  <i>20-28</i> and <i>30-43</i>) can be found.<sup id="cite_ref-officialmap_38-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-officialmap-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> Besides branches of <a href="/wiki/Burger_King" title="Burger King">Burger King</a>, <a href="/wiki/Starbucks" title="Starbucks">Starbucks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boots_UK" class="mw-redirect" title="Boots UK">Boots</a> and others, one <a href="/wiki/Airport_lounge" title="Airport lounge">airport lounge</a> is located inside the terminal.<sup id="cite_ref-officialmap_38-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-officialmap-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Airlines_and_destinations">Airlines and destinations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Luton_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Airlines and destinations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Passenger">Passenger</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-headline" id="Ground_transport">Ground transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Luton_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Ground transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Road">Road</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Luton_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Road">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The airport lies a few miles away from the <a href="/wiki/M1_motorway" title="M1 motorway">M1 motorway</a>, which runs southwards to London, northwards to <a href="/wiki/Leeds" title="Leeds">Leeds</a> and connects to the <a href="/wiki/M25_motorway" title="M25 motorway">M25 motorway</a>. The airport is linked to M1\'s Junction 10 by the dual-carriageway A1081 road. There is a short stay car park adjacent to the terminal, together with medium and long term on airport car parks to the west and east of the terminal respectively and linked to the terminal by shuttle buses. Pre-booked off airport parking is also available from several independent operators.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rail">Rail</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Luton_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Rail">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Luton_Airport_Parkway_railway_station.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Luton_Airport_Parkway_railway_station.jpg/220px-Luton_Airport_Parkway_railway_station.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="130" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Luton_Airport_Parkway_railway_station.jpg/330px-Luton_Airport_Parkway_railway_station.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Luton_Airport_Parkway_railway_station.jpg/440px-Luton_Airport_Parkway_railway_station.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="377" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Luton_Airport_Parkway_railway_station.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/First_Capital_Connect" title="First Capital Connect">First Capital Connect</a> train at <a href="/wiki/Luton_Airport_Parkway_railway_station" title="Luton Airport Parkway railway station">Luton Airport Parkway</a></div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Luton_Airport_Parkway_railway_station" title="Luton Airport Parkway railway station">Luton Airport Parkway</a> has since 1999 served the airport. It is on the <a href="/wiki/Midland_Main_Line" title="Midland Main Line">Midland Main Line</a> from <a href="/wiki/St_Pancras_railway_station" title="St Pancras railway station">London St Pancras</a>, between which, journeys take as little as 22 minutes, on services branded <a href="/wiki/East_Midlands_Railway" title="East Midlands Railway">EMR</a>.\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Thameslink_and_Great_Northern" class="mw-redirect" title="Thameslink and Great Northern">Thameslink</a> is the primary operator, with services running from the station to <a href="/wiki/Bedford_railway_station" title="Bedford railway station">Bedford</a>, <a href="/wiki/St_Albans_City_railway_station" title="St Albans City railway station">St Albans</a>, London, <a href="/wiki/Wimbledon_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Wimbledon railway station">Wimbledon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sutton_railway_station,_London" class="mw-redirect" title="Sutton railway station, London">Sutton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gatwick_Airport_railway_station" title="Gatwick Airport railway station">Gatwick Airport</a> and <a href="/wiki/Brighton_railway_station" title="Brighton railway station">Brighton</a>.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/East_Midlands_Railway" title="East Midlands Railway">East Midlands Railway</a> operate semi-fast services calling at the station hourly. These trains run south directly to London St Pancras and north to Bedford, <a href="/wiki/Wellingborough_railway_station" title="Wellingborough railway station">Wellingborough</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kettering_railway_station" title="Kettering railway station">Kettering</a>, <a href="/wiki/Corby_railway_station" title="Corby railway station">Corby</a>, <a href="/wiki/Market_Harborough_railway_station" title="Market Harborough railway station">Market Harborough</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leicester_railway_station" title="Leicester railway station">Leicester</a>, <a href="/wiki/Loughborough_railway_station" title="Loughborough railway station">Loughborough</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beeston_railway_station" title="Beeston railway station">Beeston</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nottingham_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Nottingham railway station">Nottingham</a>.</li></ul>\n<p>A shuttle bus service connects the station to the airport, a distance of just over a mile. The fare is included in pre-purchased rail tickets to/from Luton Airport (Parkway) otherwise a cash fee is charged.\n</p><p>In 2016 airport owners <span title="London Luton Airport Limited" class="rt-commentedText" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">LLAL</span> announced plans to build the <a href="/wiki/Luton_DART" title="Luton DART">Luton DART</a>, a 1.4-mile (2.3&#160;km) <a href="/wiki/Light_rail" title="Light rail">light railway</a> from the Parkway station to the airport at \xc2\xa3200 million. A planning application was submitted in Autumn 2016; it was accepted in June 2017. The link will come into passenger service by the end of 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-guardian-light-rail_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian-light-rail-69">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> Several schemes before the light rail building project were rejected, including in 2007 a proposal to replace the shuttle buses with <a href="/wiki/People_mover" title="People mover">segregated tracked transit</a> conveyors.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> From the <a href="/wiki/Midland_Main_Line" title="Midland Main Line">Midland Main Line</a> ambitious plans to build a railway spur were put forward in 2015 to reduce time, frequently, to or from central London to 20 minutes and significantly increase passenger numbers.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2016 Luton Airport commissioned a study, with the support of the <a href="/wiki/Confederation_of_British_Industry" title="Confederation of British Industry">CBI</a>, <a href="/wiki/EasyJet" title="EasyJet">easyJet</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Federation_of_Small_Businesses" title="Federation of Small Businesses">Federation of Small Businesses</a>, and the Bedfordshire and the Hertfordshire <a href="/wiki/British_Chambers_of_Commerce" title="British Chambers of Commerce">Chambers of Commerce</a> (among others) which sought to explore opportunities to expand rail services to and from the airport. The study found four fast trains per hour from central London was possible.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Negotiations are underway with the <a href="/wiki/Department_for_Transport" title="Department for Transport">Department for Transport</a> to extend the validity of the <a href="/wiki/Oyster_card" title="Oyster card">Oyster card</a> contactless ticketing system to the airport.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> Contactless bank cards (but not Oyster cards) became valid for journeys to and from London from October 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Buses">Buses</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Luton_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Buses">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bendy-bus_at_Luton_Airport_(geograph_4123189).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Bendy-bus_at_Luton_Airport_%28geograph_4123189%29.jpg/220px-Bendy-bus_at_Luton_Airport_%28geograph_4123189%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="148" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Bendy-bus_at_Luton_Airport_%28geograph_4123189%29.jpg/330px-Bendy-bus_at_Luton_Airport_%28geograph_4123189%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Bendy-bus_at_Luton_Airport_%28geograph_4123189%29.jpg/440px-Bendy-bus_at_Luton_Airport_%28geograph_4123189%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1077" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bendy-bus_at_Luton_Airport_(geograph_4123189).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <i>train2plane</i> Luton Airport bus</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Luton_to_Dunstable_Busway_route.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Luton_to_Dunstable_Busway_route.png/220px-Luton_to_Dunstable_Busway_route.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Luton_to_Dunstable_Busway_route.png/330px-Luton_to_Dunstable_Busway_route.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Luton_to_Dunstable_Busway_route.png/440px-Luton_to_Dunstable_Busway_route.png 2x" data-file-width="708" data-file-height="464" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Luton_to_Dunstable_Busway_route.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Luton_to_Dunstable_Busway" title="Luton to Dunstable Busway">Luton to Dunstable Busway</a> route</div></div></div>\n<p>Local buses connect Luton Airport with Luton town centre and other nearby places.\n</p><p>The airport is the served by the Route A of the <a href="/wiki/Luton_to_Dunstable_Busway" title="Luton to Dunstable Busway">Luton to Dunstable Busway</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Bus_rapid_transit" title="Bus rapid transit">bus rapid transit</a> route which connects the airport with Luton Town Centre and the neighbouring towns of <a href="/wiki/Dunstable" title="Dunstable">Dunstable</a>, <a href="/wiki/Houghton_Regis" title="Houghton Regis">Houghton Regis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Milton_Keynes" title="Milton Keynes">Milton Keynes</a>. The buses, operated by <a href="/wiki/Arriva_Shires_%26_Essex" title="Arriva Shires &amp; Essex">Arriva Shires &amp; Essex</a>, run on a <a href="/wiki/Guided_bus" title="Guided bus">segregated guided busway</a> track across Luton.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Conventional bus services also operate, connecting the airport with towns and cities in the region and parts of north London, including the 100, operated by Arriva, which offers an hourly daytime connection to the nearby towns of <a href="/wiki/Hitchin" title="Hitchin">Hitchin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stevenage" title="Stevenage">Stevenage</a>; <a href="/wiki/Metroline" title="Metroline">Metroline</a> service 84A; <a href="/wiki/Courtney_Buses" class="mw-redirect" title="Courtney Buses">Courtney Buses</a> coach service to <a href="/wiki/Bracknell" title="Bracknell">Bracknell</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-travel_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-travel-76">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Direct coach services to London include <a href="/wiki/Green_Line_route_757" class="mw-redirect" title="Green Line route 757">Green Line route 757</a> operated by Arriva Shires &amp; Essex and the A1 operated by <a href="/wiki/National_Express_Coaches" title="National Express Coaches">National Express</a> which operate competing services to and from <a href="/wiki/Victoria_Coach_Station" title="Victoria Coach Station">Victoria Coach Station</a>. <a href="/wiki/EasyBus" title="EasyBus">EasyBus</a> services operate towards <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_Street_station" title="Liverpool Street station">Liverpool Street station</a>. A range of longer distance National Express services linking Stansted, Heathrow and Gatwick Airports as well as destinations in the <a href="/wiki/English_Midlands" class="mw-redirect" title="English Midlands">Midlands</a> and North of England.<sup id="cite_ref-travel_76-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-travel-76">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Govia_Thameslink_Railway" title="Govia Thameslink Railway">Govia Thameslink Railway</a> provide a shuttle bus link between the airport and Luton Airport Parkway railway station. This service runs 24 hours a day - every 10 minutes from 5am to 12am and between 12am to 5am it is timed to meet each overnight train service.<sup id="cite_ref-travel_76-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-travel-76">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>There are also three services around the airport operated by <a href="/wiki/APCOA_Parking" title="APCOA Parking">APCOA Parking</a> which operate 24 hours a day serving the terminal, mid stay, long stay, and staff car parks. The service that serves the staff car park also serves the car hire centre and rental companies and all stops in between including the <a href="/wiki/Holiday_Inn_Express" title="Holiday Inn Express">Holiday Inn Express</a>, the TUI Airways HQ And the ID Unit.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (April 2016)">clarification needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> A new fleet of six <a href="/wiki/Mercedes-Benz_Citaro" title="Mercedes-Benz Citaro">Mercedes-Benz Citaro</a> buses were purchased for these operations during 2014.\n</p><p>A range of other bus services operated by off-site parking companies also serve the airport. These include Airparks, Paige Airport Parking, <a href="/wiki/Centrebus" title="Centrebus">Centrebus</a> and Coach Hire 4 U. The latter two operators provide staff shuttle buses on behalf of TUI and EasyJet.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="In_popular_culture">In popular culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Luton_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: In popular culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li>London Luton Airport appeared in two <a href="/wiki/Fly-on-the-wall" class="mw-redirect" title="Fly-on-the-wall">fly-on-the-wall</a> television documentaries, <a href="/wiki/Airline_(UK_TV_series)" class="mw-redirect" title="Airline (UK TV series)"><i>Airline</i></a> (1998) and <a href="/wiki/Luton_Airport_(TV_series)" title="Luton Airport (TV series)"><i>Luton Airport</i></a> (2005). <i>Airline</i> followed the staff of <a href="/wiki/EasyJet" title="EasyJet">EasyJet</a> at Luton and the airline\'s other bases across the country whilst the 2005 series followed the life of employees in a similar format to the show <i><a href="/wiki/Airport_(TV_series)" title="Airport (TV series)">Airport</a></i>, set in <a href="/wiki/Heathrow_Airport" title="Heathrow Airport">Heathrow Airport</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc-80th_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-80th-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>The airport was mentioned in a 1977 <a href="/wiki/Television_advert" class="mw-redirect" title="Television advert">television advert</a> for <a href="/wiki/Campari" title="Campari">Campari</a> featuring <a href="/wiki/Lorraine_Chase" title="Lorraine Chase">Lorraine Chase</a>, with the punch line "Were you truly wafted here from paradise?" \xe2\x80\x94 "Nah, Lut\'n Airport". This advert was the inspiration for the 1979 UK hit song "<a href="/wiki/Luton_Airport_(song)" title="Luton Airport (song)">Luton Airport</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Cats_UK" class="mw-redirect" title="Cats UK">Cats UK</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc-80th_11-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-80th-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>In the <a href="/wiki/Spitting_image" class="mw-redirect" title="Spitting image">Spitting image</a> TV skit for "<a href="/wiki/The_Chicken_Song" title="The Chicken Song">The Chicken Song</a>", Luton Airport appears for a brief few seconds at the beginning.</li>\n<li>The first episode of the second series of the <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a> sitcom <i><a href="/wiki/One_Foot_in_the_Grave" title="One Foot in the Grave">One Foot in the Grave</a></i> is entitled <i>In Luton Airport No-One Can Hear You Scream</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Luton Airport was mentioned in the <a href="/wiki/Piranha_Brothers" title="Piranha Brothers">Piranha Brothers</a> sketch from <i><a href="/wiki/Monty_Python%27s_Flying_Circus" title="Monty Python&#39;s Flying Circus">Monty Python\'s Flying Circus</a></i>, as being the place where one of the brothers, Dinsdale, thinks that a giant hedgehog named Spiny Norman sleeps.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>In 2011 the airport featured in an episode of the series <i>Supersize Grime</i> which focused on the cleaning of an <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A321" title="Airbus A321">Airbus A321</a> at the Monarch Aircraft Engineering hangar 127.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Accidents_and_incidents">Accidents and incidents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Luton_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Accidents and incidents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li>4 November 1949: A <a href="/wiki/Hawker_Tempest" title="Hawker Tempest">Hawker Tempest</a> single-engined piston fighter being operated by Napier Aircraft on a test flight crashed at the airport, killing the test pilot.<sup id="cite_ref-Times51531_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Times51531-81">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>23 December 1967: A <a href="/wiki/British_Aerospace_125" title="British Aerospace 125">Hawker Siddeley HS 125</a> (registration: G-AVGW) of <a href="/wiki/Court_Line" title="Court Line">Court Line</a> crashed shortly after taking off from Luton Airport, killing both pilots. The aircraft had been on a training flight. The crash occurred when the crew simulated an engine failure on takeoff. The HS 125 lost height rapidly and hit the roof of a nearby factory. This resulted in a post-crash fire.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>3 March 1974: A <a href="/wiki/Douglas_DC-7" title="Douglas DC-7">Douglas DC-7C/F</a> (registration: EI-AWG) operating an <a href="/wiki/Aer_Turas" title="Aer Turas">Aer Turas Teo</a> charter flight from Dublin landed on runway 08 just after midnight but failed to achieve <a href="/wiki/Thrust_reversal" title="Thrust reversal">reverse thrust</a>. Normal braking application also appeared to the crew to be ineffective and the emergency pneumatic brakes were applied. All main wheel tyres burst. The aircraft overran the runway and continued over the steep bank at the eastern perimeter finally coming to rest in soft ground 90 metres beyond. The situation had also been made worse by an inadvertent application of forward thrust by the crew in trying to achieve reverse thrust. Three of the six passengers and two of the four crew were injured. The aircraft was badly damaged and deemed a write-off.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AIB_Report_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AIB_Report-84">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>18 April 1974: A <a href="/wiki/BAC_One-Eleven" title="BAC One-Eleven">BAC One-Eleven</a> 518FG (registration: G-AXMJ) operating <a href="/wiki/Court_Line_Flight_95" title="Court Line Flight 95">Court Line Flight 95</a> was involved in a ground collision with <a href="/wiki/Piper_Aztec" class="mw-redirect" title="Piper Aztec">Piper PA-23 Aztec</a> (registration: G-AYDE) after the Aztec entered the active runway without clearance. The pilot of the Aztec was killed and his passenger was injured. All 91 people on board the One-Eleven successfully evacuated after take-off was aborted.</li>\n<li>21 June 1974: A <a href="/wiki/Boeing_727" title="Boeing 727">Boeing 727</a>-46 (registration: G-BAEF) operating a <a href="/wiki/Dan-Air" title="Dan-Air">Dan-Air</a> charter flight to Corfu hit the <a href="/wiki/Localizer" class="mw-redirect" title="Localizer">localiser</a> antenna while taking off, thereby rendering the runway\'s ILS inoperative. After being told by Luton air traffic control about the incident, the crew flying the aircraft elected to divert to <a href="/wiki/London_Gatwick_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="London Gatwick Airport">London Gatwick</a> where it landed safely without harming its 134 occupants (eight crew members and 126 passengers).<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> The subsequent investigation revealed that the aircraft only just became airborne at the end of the runway, and as the ground fell away to the <a href="/wiki/River_Lee_(England)" class="mw-redirect" title="River Lee (England)">Lea valley</a> below, the aircraft actually followed a downsloping course until finally gaining positive climb. The report concluded that there had been a cumulative effect of three factors \xe2\x80\x93 erosion of take-off run available; delay in starting <a href="/wiki/Rotation_(aviation)" class="mw-redirect" title="Rotation (aviation)">rotation</a>; and a very slow rate of rotation \xe2\x80\x93 as a result of the flightdeck crew\'s miscalculation of the aircraft\'s <a href="/wiki/Maximum_Takeoff_Weight" class="mw-redirect" title="Maximum Takeoff Weight">takeoff weight</a> (too high), a wrong <a href="/wiki/Jet_engine_performance" title="Jet engine performance">pressure ratio</a> for two of the aircraft\'s three engines (too low) and a sub-optimal choice of runway based on the use of outdated <a href="/wiki/Windspeed" class="mw-redirect" title="Windspeed">wind</a> information that omitted the latest update\'s <a href="/wiki/Tailwind#Tailwind_component" class="mw-redirect" title="Tailwind">tailwind component</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-AIB_Report_84-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AIB_Report-84">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>29 March 1981: A <a href="/wiki/Lockheed_JetStar" title="Lockheed JetStar">Lockheed JetStar</a> 1329 (registration: N267L) operating an inbound flight from Nigeria overran runway 08 and came to rest down the embankment beyond the eastern perimeter fence. The accident was caused because the pilot landed well past the touchdown zone in poor visibility at night. At the time runway 08 did not have an ILS. The co-pilot suffered severe spinal injuries but the commanding pilot and seven passengers escaped with only minor injuries.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>15 January 1994: A <a href="/wiki/Bell_206" title="Bell 206">Bell 206</a>B JetRanger helicopter (registration: G-BODW) rolled over on takeoff. One of the rotor blades sliced into the cabin, killing the pilot. The aircraft was badly damaged and deemed a write-off.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Future_expansion_plans">Future expansion plans</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Luton_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Future expansion plans">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Luton_Airport_from_the_air_(geograph_2962688).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Luton_Airport_from_the_air_%28geograph_2962688%29.jpg/220px-Luton_Airport_from_the_air_%28geograph_2962688%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="107" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Luton_Airport_from_the_air_%28geograph_2962688%29.jpg/330px-Luton_Airport_from_the_air_%28geograph_2962688%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Luton_Airport_from_the_air_%28geograph_2962688%29.jpg/440px-Luton_Airport_from_the_air_%28geograph_2962688%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="310" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Luton_Airport_from_the_air_(geograph_2962688).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Luton Airport may be expanded further east into adjacent parkland (top middle of the photo)</div></div></div>\n<p>In February 2019, London Luton Airport Limited announced plans to expand the airport by building a second terminal. The expansion would increase airport capacity to handle 32 million passengers per year 2039. The enlarged airport would continue to operate using the existing single runway.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>LLAL have outlined several options for the site of the new Terminal 2. Most of the proposals involve a development that will encroach upon Wigmore Valley Park, a designated <a href="/wiki/County_Wildlife_Site" title="County Wildlife Site">County Wildlife Site</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> an alternative site to the east would encroach upon the <a href="/wiki/London_Green_Belt" class="mw-redirect" title="London Green Belt">London Green Belt</a>, and a further option proposes siting a new terminal to the south of the runway.<sup id="cite_ref-llal-expansion-201902_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-llal-expansion-201902-91">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> A public consultation in October 2019 included plans for a third stop on the <a href="/wiki/Luton_DART" title="Luton DART">Luton DART</a> transit, currently under construction.<sup id="cite_ref-consultation-201910_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-consultation-201910-92">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Luton_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Airports_of_London" title="Airports of London">Airports of London</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/List_of_airports_in_the_United_Kingdom_and_the_British_Crown_Dependencies" title="List of airports in the United Kingdom and the British Crown Dependencies">List of airports in the United Kingdom and the British Crown Dependencies</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Luton" title="Transport in Luton">Transport in Luton</a></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Luton_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section:
